style="mask-image:url(&quot;data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg%20xmlns=&#x27;http://www.w3.org/2000/svg&#x27;%20viewBox=&#x27;0%200%20512%20512&#x27;%3e%3c!--!%20Font%20Awesome%20Free%206.1.1%20by%20@fontawesome%20-%20https://fontawesome.com%20License%20-%20https://fontawesome.com/license/free%20(Icons:%20CC%20BY%204.0,%20Fonts:%20SIL%20OFL%201.1,%20Code:%20MIT%20License)%20Copyright%202022%20Fonticons,%20Inc.%20--%3e%3cpath%20d=&#x27;M448%20192H64C28.65%20192%200%20220.7%200%20256v96c0%2017.67%2014.33%2032%2032%2032h32v96c0%2017.67%2014.33%2032%2032%2032h320c17.67%200%2032-14.33%2032-32v-96h32c17.67%200%2032-14.33%2032-32V256C512%20220.7%20483.3%20192%20448%20192zM384%20448H128v-96h256V448zM432%20296c-13.25%200-24-10.75-24-24c0-13.27%2010.75-24%2024-24s24%2010.73%2024%2024C456%20285.3%20445.3%20296%20432%20296zM128%2064h229.5L384%2090.51V160h64V77.25c0-8.484-3.375-16.62-9.375-22.62l-45.25-45.25C387.4%203.375%20379.2%200%20370.8%200H96C78.34%200%2064%2014.33%2064%2032v128h64V64z&#x27;/%3e%3c/svg%3e&quot;);-webkit-mask-image:url(&quot;data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg%20xmlns=&#x27;http://www.w3.org/2000/svg&#x27;%20viewBox=&#x27;0%200%20512%20512&#x27;%3e%3c!--!%20Font%20Awesome%20Free%206.1.1%20by%20@fontawesome%20-%20https://fontawesome.com%20License%20-%20https://fontawesome.com/license/free%20(Icons:%20CC%20BY%204.0,%20Fonts:%20SIL%20OFL%201.1,%20Code:%20MIT%20License)%20Copyright%202022%20Fonticons,%20Inc.%20--%3e%3cpath%20d=&#x27;M448%20192H64C28.65%20192%200%20220.7%200%20256v96c0%2017.67%2014.33%2032%2032%2032h32v96c0%2017.67%2014.33%2032%2032%2032h320c17.67%200%2032-14.33%2032-32v-96h32c17.67%200%2032-14.33%2032-32V256C512%20220.7%20483.3%20192%20448%20192zM384%20448H128v-96h256V448zM432%20296c-13.25%200-24-10.75-24-24c0-13.27%2010.75-24%2024-24s24%2010.73%2024%2024C456%20285.3%20445.3%20296%20432%20296zM128%2064h229.5L384%2090.51V160h64V77.25c0-8.484-3.375-16.62-9.375-22.62l-45.25-45.25C387.4%203.375%20379.2%200%20370.8%200H96C78.34%200%2064%2014.33%2064%2032v128h64V64z&#x27;/%3e%3c/svg%3e&quot;);mask-repeat:no-repeat;-webkit-mask-repeat:no-repeat;-webkit-mask-position:center;-webkit-mask-size:contain"></span></span></div></div></div><div class="ArticleBase-BodyContent ArticleBase-BodyContent_Article" data-testid="article-base-body-content"><div data-module="content" class="ContentModule-Wrapper"><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><img data-component="image" class="ContentParagraph-Image" data-src="http://twimgs.com/informationweek/galleries/automated/994/Syrian-Electronic-Army-Tank_01_tn.jpg?width=700&amp;auto=webp&amp;quality=80&amp;disable=upscale" src="http://twimgs.com/informationweek/galleries/automated/994/Syrian-Electronic-Army-Tank_01_tn.jpg?width=700&amp;auto=webp&amp;quality=80&amp;disable=upscale" loading="lazy" alt="The Syrian Electronic Army: 9 Things We Know" title="The Syrian Electronic Army: 9 Things We Know"/><p class="ContentParagraph-Caption">The Syrian Electronic Army: 9 Things We Know</p><br/><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">(click image for larger view)</span><br/><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">The Syrian Electronic Army: 9 Things We Know</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"> Who&#x27;s launching online attacks against your network? How can you better detect those attacks and -- if an attack turns out to be successful -- identify what was stolen?</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">Enabling businesses to answer those questions is the premise of a cloud-based service announced Tuesday by security startup CrowdStrike. Dubbed Falcon, the big-data &quot;active defense platform&quot; is designed to identify intrusions in real time, attribute attacks – correlate with a known group of attackers – and help businesses block attacks or even engage in counterintelligence or deception by feeding attackers fake information.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">&quot;This is the real-time damage assessment that no one is doing today,&quot; said </span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://www.informationweek.com/security/attacks/shady-rat-attack-hit-72-organizations/231300162">Dmitri Alperovitch</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">, the co-founder and CTO of CrowdStrike, speaking by phone. &quot;It shows you who the adversary is, what did they do [on your network], what did they take, which commands did they execute?&quot; The service works in part by running a small (400 KB) &quot;sensor&quot; on Windows 7 and Mac OS X systems, bolstered by DNS, email and API sensors on servers, to track the types of attacks that are being launched. CrowdStrike then correlates attack information with intelligence that the company gathers on attack groups.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><span class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_bold">[ NSA whistleblower&#x27;s accusations deepen. Read </span></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link ContentText-BodyTextChunk_bold" target="_blank" href="http://www.informationweek.com/security/privacy/snowden-says-us-hacking-chinese-civilian/240156625?itc=edit_in_body_cross">Snowden Says U.S. Hacking Chinese Civilians Since 2009</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><span class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_bold">. ]</span></span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">As highlighted by </span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://www.informationweek.com/security/attacks/spear-phishing-attacks-on-the-rise/230500025">successful spear-phishing attacks</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"> against everyone from security giant RSA to the White House, stopping every last information security attack might be impossible. So-called </span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://www.informationweek.com/security/cybercrime/advanced-persistent-threats-get-more-res/232600562">advanced persistent threat (APT) groups</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"> often use fake emails and attachments to infect targeted PCs and steal data, oftentimes without end users or security teams being aware. Once attackers infect a single PC, unless they&#x27;re detected, they can lurk in corporate networks indefinitely: telecommunications giant </span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://www.informationweek.com/security/attacks/8-lessons-from-nortels-10-year-security/232601092">Nortel</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"> was compromised for 10 years, </span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://www.informationweek.com/security/government/china-tied-to-3-year-hack-of-defense-con/240154064">defense contractor QinetiQ</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"> for three years.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">Such attacks are cheap to build and inexpensive to launch. Even if only one attack out of every 100 or 1,000 attempts succeeds, that might equal success for attackers. Given that reality, CrowdStrike&#x27;s play is to help businesses identify not just when they&#x27;ve been attacked, but also who stole the information, what they stole and why they targeted the business in the first place -- what&#x27;s their bigger goal?</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">&quot;The problem you&#x27;ve had for the past six to seven years is the emergence of targeted attackers, and for them, it doesn&#x27;t mater how many layers of defense you put in place; what they want is you,&quot; said Alperovitch. &quot;They want money, national secrets, intellectual property, and they&#x27;re going to worm their way in, because the return on that investment is gigantic.&quot;</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">Could defenders gain an edge by better understanding their attackers? &quot;From an adversary perspective, we really focus on the targeted attackers,&quot; said Alperovitch. &quot;We&#x27;re tracking lots of nation-state-sponsored groups that are working to penetrate companies,&quot; he said, and &quot;understanding their campaigns, and tradecraft, as well as who they&#x27;re targeting.&quot;</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">CrowdStrike has grouped attackers into &quot;adversary groups&quot; -- to date, about 48 in total -- named for country characteristics: &quot;pandas&quot; for groups operating from China; &quot;cats&quot; as in Persian cats for Iran; &quot;bears&quot; for Russia; &quot;saints&quot; for Georgia; and &quot;tigers&quot; for India. &quot;Some in the community refer to the adversary by the malware detection name from a specific antivirus vendor, e.g. Hydraq,&quot; said Adam Meyers, director of intelligence at CrowdStrike, in a </span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://www.crowdstrike.com/blog/whois-anchor-panda/index.html">blog post</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">, referring to the name of the malware used in the so-called </span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://www.informationweek.com/security/attacks/google-aurora-hack-was-chinese-counteres/240155268">Aurora attacks</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"> against Google. &quot;This is sometimes useful, but when the adversary is using a malware that is detected as Generic.Downloader.234, you have a much harder time communicating,&quot; Meyers said.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">CrowdStrike recommends that businesses use its intelligence on online adversaries to identify and focus on the attackers they&#x27;re most likely to face. &quot;For example, if you&#x27;re in the financial service industry, you&#x27;ll care about Big Panda, which is going after financial services firms, but not Karma Panda that&#x27;s going after dissident groups,&quot; said Alperovitch. &quot;If you&#x27;re trying to go after everyone and defend against everything, you&#x27;re really defending against nothing.&quot;</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">For instance, one group that CrowdStrike has been tracking -- dubbed Anchor Panda -- has launched 124 attacks over the past six months, many of which appear to be aimed in part at </span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://www.informationweek.com/security/attacks/chinese-hackers-stole-us-military-secret/240155624">building out deep-sea capabilities</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">. Adam Meyers, head of intelligence for Crowdstrike, recently told </span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><span class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_italic">The New Yorker</span></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"> that the information being targeted by the group bears more than a passing resemblance to </span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://www.newyorker.com/reporting/2013/05/20/130520fa_fact_seabrook">China&#x27;s five-year plan for modernizing its infrastructure</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">Once businesses have identified the group behind an attack, or used new intelligence to identify previously unidentified attacks that were successful as well as what was stolen, what happens next? According to Alperovitch, &quot;if you want to work with the government, we can help with that as well, on our services side,&quot; which is headed by </span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://www.informationweek.com/security/attacks/china-hack-attacks-play-offense-or-defen/240150482">Shawn Henry</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">, whose prior job was serving as the executive assistant director of the FBI&#x27;s criminal, cyber, response and services branch. &quot;Or you take the attribution and take legal action against that individual or the company,&quot; he said. &quot;A lot of companies are multinationals, so you can actually sue them in the United States -- or in a jurisdiction of your choosing overseas, and get criminal damages or injunctive relief for stolen information.&quot;</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">Alperovitch said that when it comes to responding to hack attacks, there can be strength in numbers: &quot;If you&#x27;re one company going up against China, you&#x27;re going to be afraid of retaliation, of your business being shut out of China. But if you&#x27;re in a band of 20 or 30 Fortune 100 companies, China can&#x27;t really retaliate; it needs them all.&quot;</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">&quot;Ultimately we&#x27;ll only solve this problem together, not individually trying to build castles to protect ourselves,&quot; said Alperovitch. &quot;That model hasn&#x27;t worked in the physical world in over 400 years, and certainly not in cyber space.&quot;</span></p></div></div><div class="SocialShare"><div data-component="social-share" class="SocialShare SocialShare_variant_button ArticleBase-SocialShare ArticleBase-SocialShare_second"><a
